{"code":1,"isDone":false,"toInsertArticleList":[{"createdTime":"2021-04-08 01:37:49","updatedTime":"2021-04-08 01:37:49","title":"How to Cook a Basic Omelette","link":"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-a-Basic-Omelette","description":"<div class=\"mw-parser-output\">\n <p>You may have heard that the true test of a cook is whether or not they can make a good basic omelette. Fortunately, as long as you follow a few simple guidelines, you can easily whip up an inexpensive, filling dish that tastes like a pro made it. Fold your omelette in half for a traditional option or roll it up it for a softer, French-style dish. Feel free to customize your basic omelette by adding your favorite fillings just before you fold or roll it. </p> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Cook-a-Basic-Omelette&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1\" title=\"Edit section: Ingredients\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Ingredients\">Ingredients</span></h2> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Cook-a-Basic-Omelette&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2\" title=\"Edit section: Folded Diner-Style Omelette\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Folded-Diner-Style-Omelette\">Folded Diner-Style Omelette</span></h3> \n <ul>\n  <li>2 to 3 eggs</li> \n  <li>of oil, such as vegetable, sunflower, canola, or olive oil</li> \n  <li>1 teaspoon (4 g) of butter</li> \n  <li>Salt and pepper to taste</li>\n </ul> \n <p><i>Makes 1 omelette</i> </p> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Cook-a-Basic-Omelette&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3\" title=\"Edit section: French-Style Rolled Omelette\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"French-Style-Rolled-Omelette\">French-Style Rolled Omelette</span></h3> \n <ul>\n  <li>3 large eggs</li> \n  <li>Salt and pepper to taste</li> \n  <li>1 tablespoon (14 g) of unsalted butter, plus more for serving</li> \n  <li>1 tablespoon (3 g) of chopped fresh herbs, such as chives, tarragon, or parsley, optional</li>\n </ul> \n <p><i>Makes 1 omelette</i> </p> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Cook-a-Basic-Omelette&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4\" title=\"Edit section: Steps\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Steps\">Steps</span></h2> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Cook-a-Basic-Omelette&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5\" title=\"Edit section: Making a Folded Diner-Style Omelette\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Making-a-Folded-Diner-Style-Omelette\">Making a Folded Diner-Style Omelette</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Whisk 2 or 3 eggs with salt and pepper. Crack as many eggs as you'd like into a small bowl or dish. Then, sprinkle in salt and pepper according to your taste. Take a whisk or a fork and beat the eggs until the mixture is a uniform yellow color. Whisk for at least 10 seconds so the omelette is consistent in texture.<sup id=\"_ref-1\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 1\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-a-Basic-Omelette#_note-1\">[1]</a></sup><br /><br />\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Cook-a-Basic-Omelette-Step-2-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Cook a Basic Omelette Step 2 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/b/b2/Cook-a-Basic-Omelette-Step-2-Version-2.jpg/aid585991-v4-728px-Cook-a-Basic-Omelette-Step-2-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"410\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>You could also flavor the omelet with dry seasonings of your choice. Sprinkle a little curry powder or cajun seasoning, for instance.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Melt of oil and 1 teaspoon (4 g) of butter in a skillet. Set an nonstick skillet on the stove and turn the burner to medium-low. Put of oil and 1 teaspoon (4 g) of butter into the pan so they melt and coat the bottom of the skillet.<sup id=\"_ref-2\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 2\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-a-Basic-Omelette#_note-2\">[2]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Cook-a-Basic-Omelette-Step-1-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Cook a Basic Omelette Step 1 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/6/6c/Cook-a-Basic-Omelette-Step-1-Version-2.jpg/aid585991-v4-728px-Cook-a-Basic-Omelette-Step-1-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"410\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Use your favorite oil, such as vegetable, sunflower, canola, or olive oil.</li> \n    <li>The oil prevents the butter from burning in the skillet. If you prefer, you could use all butter or all oil instead.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Pour the beaten eggs into the pan. Once the skillet is hot and the butter is foaming, slowly pour the beaten eggs into it. Hold the handle and slowly tilt the pan until the egg mixture coats the entire surface of the skillet.<sup id=\"_ref-3\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 3\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-a-Basic-Omelette#_note-3\">[3]</a></sup><br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Keep the burner at medium-low heat so the omelette cooks evenly. If the burner is up too high, the omelette will become rubbery.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Cook the omelette and tilt the pan mixture until the omelette's almost set. Leave the eggs to cook for about 20 seconds before stirring the edges of the skillet with a rubber spatula. Scoot the curds along the edges towards the center of the skillet. Then, tilt the skillet so the egg mixture runs to the empty edges of the skillet.<sup id=\"_ref-4\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 4\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-a-Basic-Omelette#_note-4\">[4]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Cook-a-Basic-Omelette-Step-4-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Cook a Basic Omelette Step 4 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/0/0e/Cook-a-Basic-Omelette-Step-4-Version-2.jpg/aid585991-v4-728px-Cook-a-Basic-Omelette-Step-4-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"410\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Cook the omelette until it's set, but still slightly glossy on top. This should take about 1 minute.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Add your choice of fillings if you want to make a heartier omelette. Although you don't need to add any fillings to a basic omelette, it's easy to customize one. Sprinkle about 1/3 cup (78 g) of fillings over 1/2 of the omelette. You could use:<sup id=\"_ref-5\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 5\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-a-Basic-Omelette#_note-5\">[5]</a></sup><br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Shredded cheese, such as cheddar, monterey jack, or colby jack</li> \n    <li>Saut√©ed vegetables, such as mushrooms, bell peppers, or onions</li> \n    <li>Diced cooked meat, such as ham, sausage, chorizo, or bacon</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Turn off the burner and fold the omelette in half. Take a rubber spatula and gently lift up the edges of the omelette on 1 side. Then, slide the spatula under the omelette and lift 1/2 of the omelette over to the other side. Slide the omelette onto a serving plate and enjoy it while it's hot.<sup id=\"_ref-6\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 6\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-a-Basic-Omelette#_note-6\">[6]</a></sup><br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Although the omelette has the best texture immediately after cooking, you can refrigerate leftovers in an airtight container for up to 3 days.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Cook-a-Basic-Omelette&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6\" title=\"Edit section: Making a French-Style Rolled Omelette\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Making-a-French-Style-Rolled-Omelette\">Making a French-Style Rolled Omelette</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Beat 3 eggs in a bowl with salt and pepper. Crack 3 large eggs into a bowl and use a whisk or fork to beat the eggs. Keep beating until the yolks are incorporated into the whites and the eggs are a uniform yellow color. Whisk for at least 10 seconds to ensure that the omelette has a consistent texture and color.<sup id=\"_ref-7\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 7\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-a-Basic-Omelette#_note-7\">[7]</a></sup> (3 g) of finely chopped fresh herbs, such as chives, tarragon, or parsley to the beaten eggs.}}<br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Avoid beating the eggs until they become foamy or they won't cook evenly.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Melt 1 tablespoon (14 g) of butter in a nonstick skillet over medium-high heat. Set an nonstick skillet on the stove and put (14 g) of unsalted butter into it. Turn the burner to medium-high and tilt the pan a little so the butter coats the skillet as it melts.<sup id=\"_ref-8\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 8\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-a-Basic-Omelette#_note-8\">[8]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Cook-a-Basic-Omelette-Step-8-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Cook a Basic Omelette Step 8 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/a/a1/Cook-a-Basic-Omelette-Step-8-Version-2.jpg/aid585991-v4-728px-Cook-a-Basic-Omelette-Step-8-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"410\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>You could also use a seasoned carbon steel pan.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Pour the eggs into the skillet and stir them until they're softly set. Slowly pour the eggs into the hot skillet and begin shaking the pan gently to keep the eggs moving. Use a spatula or chopsticks to stir the eggs in the skillet for about 1 minute. This breaks up the curds so you get a smoother, softer omelette.<sup id=\"_ref-9\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 9\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-a-Basic-Omelette#_note-9\">[9]</a></sup><br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Ensure that you stir the edges of the omelette since these usually cook faster than the eggs in the center of the skillet.</li> \n    <li>Although you can add fillings, keep them to a minimum so the omelette is easy to roll.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Roll the omelette over itself by intervals. The omelette will probably crack if you try to roll it tightly. Instead, take a spatula and loosen the edges of the omelette. Tilt the handle of the skillet up while you lift the closest edge of the omelette up. Roll it towards the center of the omelette away from the handle. Keep lifting and rolling about of the omelette until you've rolled it to the side of the skillet that's opposite from the handle.<sup id=\"_ref-10\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 10\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-a-Basic-Omelette#_note-10\">[10]</a></sup><br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If you're struggling to roll the omelette with the spatula, try using chopsticks for greater control.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Slide the rolled omelette onto a plate so the seam is facing down. Bring your serving plate over to the skillet. Slowly tilt the skillet up and over the plate so the rolled omelette lands on the plate seam-side down.<sup id=\"_ref-11\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 11\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-a-Basic-Omelette#_note-11\">[11]</a></sup><br /><br />\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Cook-a-Basic-Omelette-Step-11.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Cook a Basic Omelette Step 11.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/7/7d/Cook-a-Basic-Omelette-Step-11.jpg/aid585991-v4-728px-Cook-a-Basic-Omelette-Step-11.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"410\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Serve the omelette while it's hot. You could garnish it with more fresh herbs if you like.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <p><br /> </p> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Cook-a-Basic-Omelette&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7\" title=\"Edit section: Video\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Video\">Video</span></h2> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Cook-a-Basic-Omelette&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8\" title=\"Edit section: Tips\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Tips\">Tips</span></h2> \n <ul>\n  <li>To make an omelette for a few people, choose the folded omelette and stuff it with your favorite fillings, such as <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Make-a-Mushroom-Omelette\" title=\"Make a Mushroom Omelette\">mushrooms</a>, <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Make-a-Cheese-Omelette\" title=\"Make a Cheese Omelette\">cheese</a>, or <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Make-a-Ham-and-Cheese-Omelet\" title=\"Make a Ham and Cheese Omelet\">ham and cheese</a>.</li>\n </ul> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Cook-a-Basic-Omelette&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9\" title=\"Edit section: Things You'll Need\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span id=\"Things-You'll-Need\"></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Things-You.27ll-Need\">Things You'll Need</span></h2> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Cook-a-Basic-Omelette&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10\" title=\"Edit section: Folded Diner-Style Omelette\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Folded-Diner-Style-Omelette_2\">Folded Diner-Style Omelette</span></h3> \n <ul>\n  <li>Measuring spoons</li> \n  <li>Small bowl</li> \n  <li>Whisk or fork</li> \n  <li>nonstick skillet</li> \n  <li>Spatula</li> \n  <li>Serving plate</li>\n </ul> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" fork</li> \n  <li>nonstick skillet</li> \n  <li>Spatula</li> \n  <li>Serving plate</li>\n </ul> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a +0000","feedId":44,"bgimg":"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/b/b2/Cook-a-Basic-Omelette-Step-2-Version-2.jpg/aid585991-v4-728px-Cook-a-Basic-Omelette-Step-2-Version-2.jpg","linkMd5":"826470400a067b53b7bc80dc80ef2cda","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn11@2020_6/2021/04/07/17-37-50-385_751562b45e1ff7b6.webp","destWidth":728,"destHeight":410,"sourceBytes":51424,"destBytes":27854,"author":"","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/b/b2/Cook-a-Basic-Omelette-Step-2-Version-2.jpg/aid585991-v4-728px-Cook-a-Basic-Omelette-Step-2-Version-2.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn11@2020_6/2021/04/07/17-37-50-385_751562b45e1ff7b6.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/6/6c/Cook-a-Basic-Omelette-Step-1-Version-2.jpg/aid585991-v4-728px-Cook-a-Basic-Omelette-Step-1-Version-2.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn16@2020_5/2021/04/07/17-38-24-236_43be87cd1f529b9b.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/0/0e/Cook-a-Basic-Omelette-Step-4-Version-2.jpg/aid585991-v4-728px-Cook-a-Basic-Omelette-Step-4-Version-2.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn72@2020_2/2021/04/07/17-38-23-770_70b5a43d4355e8f7.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/a/a1/Cook-a-Basic-Omelette-Step-8-Version-2.jpg/aid585991-v4-728px-Cook-a-Basic-Omelette-Step-8-Version-2.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn67@2020_1/2021/04/07/17-38-23-745_f2601d07dc167230.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/7/7d/Cook-a-Basic-Omelette-Step-11.jpg/aid585991-v4-728px-Cook-a-Basic-Omelette-Step-11.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn84@2020_3/2021/04/07/17-38-23-845_57ad861bc2230c64.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1617817069951},{"createdTime":"2021-04-08 01:37:49","updatedTime":"2021-04-08 01:37:49","title":"How to Copy and Paste a Link","link":"https://www.wikihow.com/Copy-and-Paste-a-Link","description":"<div class=\"mw-parser-output\">\n <p>Links to online articles and websites improve the richness of online text and increase its search engine optimization. You can reference almost any website by copying and pasting the link into your email, text message, or document. The procedure may differ slightly depending upon the computer, device or program you are using. If the address is very long, you can use a link shortening service. </p> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Copy-and-Paste-a-Link&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1\" title=\"Edit section: Steps\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Steps\">Steps</span></h2> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Copy-and-Paste-a-Link&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2\" title=\"Edit section: Windows and Mac\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Windows-and-Mac\">Windows and Mac</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Copy and paste an address from the address bar. If you want to share or save a website you're visiting, you can copy the address from the address bar of your browser:\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-1-Version-6.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Copy and Paste a Link Step 1 Version 6.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/3/32/Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-1-Version-6.jpg/aid3928015-v4-728px-Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-1-Version-6.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Click the address in your browser. This may reveal the entire address if parts were hidden while browsing.</li> \n    <li>Select the entire address if it isn't already. Usually the address will automatically be selected when you click it. If it isn't, press / to select the entire thing.</li> \n    <li>Copy the selected address by right-clicking the selection and clicking \"Copy,\" or by pressing /.</li> \n    <li>Place your cursor where you want to paste the link and press /.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Find the link you want to copy. You can copy links from websites, emails, Word documents, and pretty much any other program.\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-2-Version-6.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Copy and Paste a Link Step 2 Version 6.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/3/3d/Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-2-Version-6.jpg/aid3928015-v4-728px-Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-2-Version-6.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Text links in web pages and emails are often underlined and a different color than the surrounding text. Many links are buttons and pictures.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Right-click the link.<sup id=\"_ref-1\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 1\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Copy-and-Paste-a-Link#_note-1\">[1]</a></sup> If the link is a picture, right-clicking the picture will provide the Copy option.\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-3-Version-6.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Copy and Paste a Link Step 3 Version 6.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/3/3c/Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-3-Version-6.jpg/aid3928015-v4-728px-Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-3-Version-6.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If you're on a Mac with a single mouse button, hold and click to open the right-click menu.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Select the \"Copy link\" option. When a link is copied, it is sent to your clipboard to be pasted elsewhere.<sup id=\"_ref-2\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 2\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Copy-and-Paste-a-Link#_note-2\">[2]</a></sup> The clipboard can only store a single link at a time. The wording of this option will vary depending on what program you are using. Below are some common examples:\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-4-Version-6.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Copy and Paste a Link Step 4 Version 6.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/3/39/Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-4-Version-6.jpg/aid3928015-v4-728px-Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-4-Version-6.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Chrome - \"Copy link address\"</li> \n    <li>Firefox - \"Copy Link Location\"</li> \n    <li>Internet Explorer - \"Copy shortcut\"</li> \n    <li>Safari - \"Copy Link\"</li> \n    <li>Word - \"Copy Hyperlink\"</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Place your cursor where you want to paste the link. Once your link is copied, you can paste it anywhere you can type.<sup id=\"_ref-3\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 3\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Copy-and-Paste-a-Link#_note-3\">[3]</a></sup> Click to place your cursor wherever you want to paste the link.\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-5-Version-5.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Copy and Paste a Link Step 5 Version 5.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/8/81/Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-5-Version-5.jpg/aid3928015-v4-728px-Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-5-Version-5.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>You can paste the link anywhere you can type, including in emails, Word documents, your browser's address bar, Facebook chats, and more.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Paste the link. There are several ways you can paste your copied link:\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-6-Version-5.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Copy and Paste a Link Step 6 Version 5.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/c/c3/Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-6-Version-5.jpg/aid3928015-v4-728px-Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-6-Version-5.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Right-click wherever your cursor is and select \"Paste.\"</li> \n    <li>Press (Windows) or (Mac).</li> \n    <li>Click the Edit menu (if present) and select \"Paste.\" Not all programs have a visible Edit menu.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Paste the link as a hyperlink with different text. Some programs, such as blogs, email programs, and word processors, allow you to change the text that displays instead of showing the whole link address. This lets you create a link with a sentence or word:<sup id=\"_ref-4\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 4\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Copy-and-Paste-a-Link#_note-4\">[4]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-7-Version-5.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Copy and Paste a Link Step 7 Version 5.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/2/2f/Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-7-Version-5.jpg/aid3928015-v4-728px-Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-7-Version-5.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Place your cursor where you want the hyperlink to go.</li> \n    <li>Click the \"Insert Hyperlink\" button. This may be below the text form, or in the Insert menu (word processors). The button often has a chainlink icon.</li> \n    <li>Type what you want to appear in the \"Text to display\" field. This is what will appear as the clickable link.</li> \n    <li>Paste the link in the \"Address,\" \"URL,\" or \"Link to\" field. Click in the field and press (Windows) or (Mac) to paste the copied link.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Copy-and-Paste-a-Link&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3\" title=\"Edit section: Mobile Devices\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Mobile-Devices\">Mobile Devices</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Find the link you want to copy. You can copy links from web browsers, emails, and many other apps. Links may be traditional text links or may be a picture.\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-8-Version-5.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Copy and Paste a Link Step 8 Version 5.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/2/2d/Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-8-Version-5.jpg/aid3928015-v4-728px-Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-8-Version-5.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>The process for this is very similar regardless of what type of mobile device you're using (Android, iPhone, iPad, Windows mobile, etc.)</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Press and hold the link you want to copy. Once you've found the link, press and hold it until a new menu appears. It may take a few moments for the menu to show up.<sup id=\"_ref-5\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 5\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Copy-and-Paste-a-Link#_note-5\">[5]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-9-Version-5.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Copy and Paste a Link Step 9 Version 5.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/3/3b/Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-9-Version-5.jpg/aid3928015-v4-728px-Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-9-Version-5.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div></li> \n  <li>Tap the \"Copy\" option. The wording for this will vary depending on the app you are using. Look for wording similar to these examples:\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-10-Version-5.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Copy and Paste a Link Step 10 Version 5.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/9/9f/Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-10-Version-5.jpg/aid3928015-v4-728px-Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-10-Version-5.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Copy</li> \n    <li>Copy link address</li> \n    <li>Copy link URL</li> \n    <li>Copy address</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Place your cursor where you want to paste the link. Once you've copied the link, you can paste it anywhere you can type. Tap the text field to place your cursor.\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-11-Version-5.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Copy and Paste a Link Step 11 Version 5.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/a/a1/Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-11-Version-5.jpg/aid3928015-v4-728px-Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-11-Version-5.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div></li> \n  <li>Press and hold your finger on your cursor. Release your finger after a moment. A new menu will appear.\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-12-Version-5.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Copy and Paste a Link Step 12 Version 5.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/1/14/Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-12-Version-5.jpg/aid3928015-v4-728px-Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-12-Version-5.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If you're using an iOS device (iPhone, iPad, iPod Touch), release your finger once the magnifier lens appears.</li> \n    <li>If you're using an Android device, release your finger when the indicator under the cursor appears.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Tap \"Paste\" to paste your copied link. You'll see the \"Paste\" option in the menu that appears. Tapping \"Paste\" will paste the copied address into the text field.\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-13-Version-4.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Copy and Paste a Link Step 13 Version 4.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/3/3d/Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-13-Version-4.jpg/aid3928015-v4-728px-Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-13-Version-4.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div></li> \n  <li>Copy and paste a link from a text message (Android). If you've received a text message with a link on your Android device, you may have to do a little more work to copy it, especially if there is other text with it. Not all Android messaging apps will function the same:\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-14-Version-4.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Copy and Paste a Link Step 14 Version 4.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/2/24/Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-14-Version-4.jpg/aid3928015-v4-728px-Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-14-Version-4.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Press and hold on the message that contains the link.</li> \n    <li>Tap the \"Copy\" button that appears. It may just be an icon of two pages stacked on each other at the top of the screen.</li> \n    <li>Paste the copied text where you want to paste the link, and then manually delete any extra text that came with the original message.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Copy-and-Paste-a-Link&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4\" title=\"Edit section: Using a Link Shortener\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Using-a-Link-Shortener\">Using a Link Shortener</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Use a link shortener service when you need to text or tweet a link. Website addresses can get really long, especially for pages buried deep in a site. Link shortener services allow you to generate a short version of a long address that can easily be texted, tweeted, or otherwise shared.\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-15-Version-4.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Copy and Paste a Link Step 15 Version 4.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/8/84/Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-15-Version-4.jpg/aid3928015-v4-728px-Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-15-Version-4.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div></li> \n  <li>Copy the link you want to share. Use the methods outlined above to copy the link you want to shorten and share.\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-16-Version-4.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Copy and Paste a Link Step 16 Version 4.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/1/16/Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-16-Version-4.jpg/aid3928015-v4-728px-Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-16-Version-4.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div></li> \n  <li>Visit a link shortener website. There are several services available for shortening links, and most work very similarly:\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-17-Version-4.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Copy and Paste a Link Step 17 Version 4.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/1/19/Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-17-Version-4.jpg/aid3928015-v4-728px-Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-17-Version-4.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>bit.ly</li> \n    <li>goo.gl</li> \n    <li>ow.ly</li> \n    <li>tinyurl.com</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Paste your long link into the field on the shortener site. Click the field and press /, or long-press and select \"Paste,\" to paste your long link into the field on the shortener site.\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-18-Version-4.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Copy and Paste a Link Step 18 Version 4.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/6/64/Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-18-Version-4.jpg/aid3928015-v4-728px-Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-18-Version-4.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div></li> \n  <li>Tap or click the \"Shorten\" or \"Shrink\" button to generate a new link. You'll be presented with a short version of the link that uses the service's format instead of the original site's.\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-19-Version-4.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Copy and Paste a Link Step 19 Version 4.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/5/5a/Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-19-Version-4.jpg/aid3928015-v4-728px-Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-19-Version-4.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div></li> \n  <li>Copy the shortened link. You can copy like you would a regular link using the methods above, or tap or click the \"Copy\" button that some sites display.\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-20-Version-4.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Copy and Paste a Link Step 20 Version 4.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/8/85/Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-20-Version-4.jpg/aid3928015-v4-728px-Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-20-Version-4.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div></li> \n  <li>Paste your shortened link. Now that your shortened link has been copied, you can paste it just like you would any other link. You may want to give some context for the link, since it won't be apparent what it's for by looking at the shortened address.\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-21-Version-4.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Copy and Paste a Link Step 21 Version 4.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/2/23/Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-21-Version-4.jpg/aid3928015-v4-728px-Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-21-Version-4.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div></li>\n </ol> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Copy-and-Paste-a-Link&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5\" title=\"Edit section: Video\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Video\">Video</span></h2> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Copy-and-Paste-a-Link&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6\" title=\"Edit section: References\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"References\">References</span></h2> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span /8/84/Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-15-Version-4.jpg/aid3928015-v4-728px-Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-15-Version-4.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn47@2020_6/2021/04/07/17-38-24-428_6c840d63b665d9ce.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/1/16/Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-16-Version-4.jpg/aid3928015-v4-728px-Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-16-Version-4.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn48@2020_2/2021/04/07/17-38-23-748_8155fb9ec189d04c.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/1/19/Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-17-Version-4.jpg/aid3928015-v4-728px-Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-17-Version-4.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn28@2020_2/2021/04/07/17-38-23-733_c378f8af8f2ea5e8.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/6/64/Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-18-Version-4.jpg/aid3928015-v4-728px-Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-18-Version-4.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn28@2020_2/2021/04/07/17-38-24-336_9d51bfc03409a433.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/5/5a/Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-19-Version-4.jpg/aid3928015-v4-728px-Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-19-Version-4.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn79@2020_2/2021/04/07/17-38-23-716_a02cf1ec9de85c0f.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/8/85/Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-20-Version-4.jpg/aid3928015-v4-728px-Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-20-Version-4.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn88@2020_4/2021/04/07/17-38-23-618_8eaf8caf5f63ac3c.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/2/23/Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-21-Version-4.jpg/aid3928015-v4-728px-Copy-and-Paste-a-Link-Step-21-Version-4.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn44@2020_2/2021/04/07/17-38-23-591_be7710753efafa08.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1617817069954},{"createdTime":"2021-04-08 01:37:49","updatedTime":"2021-04-08 01:37:49","title":"How to Criticize Constructively","link":"https://www.wikihow.com/Criticize-Constructively","description":"<div class=\"mw-parser-output\">\n <p>Giving constructive, critical feedback is an art. It‚Äôs a way to encourage positive behavior without blaming or attacking the person you‚Äôre criticizing. If you‚Äôre going to master the skills required to give constructive criticism, it‚Äôs essential that you maintain a positive tone and focus on clear, achievable objectives. While there are dozens of ways to give constructive criticism, remember that everyone is different and you should customize the way you give feedback based on what you know about the person you‚Äôre talking to. </p> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Criticize-Constructively&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1\" title=\"Edit section: Steps\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Steps\">Steps</span></h2> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Criticize-Constructively&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2\" title=\"Edit section: Give constructive criticism when you have a good reason to do so.\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Give-constructive-criticism-when-you-have-a-good-reason-to-do-so.\">Give constructive criticism when you have a good reason to do so.</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Before you criticize, ask yourself, ‚ÄúWhat is the point here?‚Äù Identifying what you‚Äôre hoping to get out of the conversation will help you figure out to where you want to focus the chat. If you don‚Äôt have a clear objective in mind, you risk overloading the person with excess information, or making them feel like you‚Äôre boxing them in.<sup id=\"_ref-1\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 1\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Criticize-Constructively#_note-1\">[1]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Criticize-Constructively-Step-1-Version-7.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Criticize Constructively Step 1 Version 7.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/9/91/Criticize-Constructively-Step-1-Version-7.jpg/aid15271-v4-728px-Criticize-Constructively-Step-1-Version-7.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>You may have a specific behavior you want to see changed. For example, your goal may be to get an employee to stop breaking a company rule, or for a student to stop shouting out over classmates when they‚Äôre excited.</li> \n    <li>Your goal could also be to help somebody improve. For example, you might want to show a co-worker a better way to communicate with customers, or help a teacher you manage get better at classroom management.</li> \n    <li>If you don‚Äôt have a good answer to the question, ‚ÄúWhat is the point here?‚Äù you may not need to criticize anything. Having a criticism in mind doesn‚Äôt mean it needs to be shared.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Criticize-Constructively&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3\" title=\"Edit section: Be conscious of your tone.\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Be-conscious-of-your-tone.\">Be conscious of your tone.</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>What you say matters, but how you say it matters a lot, too. If the other person feels like you‚Äôre coming from a healthy, friendly place, they‚Äôre going to be much more likely to pick up what you‚Äôre putting down. It‚Äôs hard to improve if you think you‚Äôre being attacked for making a mistake, so keep the voice of your volume down, maintain relaxed body language, and try to make the other person feel respected and appreciated with the tone of your voice.<sup id=\"_ref-2\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 2\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Criticize-Constructively#_note-2\">[2]</a></sup> \n   <ul>\n    <li>There may be occasions where a harsh or serious tone is called-for. If you catch your child playing with fireworks, or you have an employee cursing in front of customers, it‚Äôs really important that you emphasize how serious the issue is.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Criticize-Constructively&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4\" title=\"Edit section: Have the conversation in private.\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Have-the-conversation-in-private.\">Have the conversation in private.</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Praise in public and criticize in private for the best results. Nobody likes to hear that they aren‚Äôt doing a perfect job, so have this conversation privately to put the person you‚Äôre criticizing at ease. You could invite the person into your office with a smile on your face, or ask someone to swing by during lunch for a quick chat.<sup id=\"_ref-3\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 3\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Criticize-Constructively#_note-3\">[3]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Criticize-Constructively-Step-2-Version-7.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Criticize Constructively Step 2 Version 7.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/9/94/Criticize-Constructively-Step-2-Version-7.jpg/aid15271-v4-728px-Criticize-Constructively-Step-2-Version-7.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If you criticize someone in front of other people, they may feel like they‚Äôre being attacked or publicly-shamed. The odds are much higher that you have a productive conversation if nobody else is around to witness it.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Criticize-Constructively&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5\" title=\"Edit section: Lead with something complimentary.\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Lead-with-something-complimentary.\">Lead with something complimentary.</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Find something awesome to say about the other person. If you‚Äôre critiquing someone‚Äôs sales numbers, start by explaining that you see the hard work they‚Äôre putting in. If you‚Äôre going to critique someone for being rude, start by sharing how you appreciate their passion. Leading with a positive note will put the other person in a more receptive headspace before you get to the heart of the issue.<sup id=\"_ref-4\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 4\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Criticize-Constructively#_note-4\">[4]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Criticize-Constructively-Step-3-Version-7.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Criticize Constructively Step 3 Version 7.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/9/9e/Criticize-Constructively-Step-3-Version-7.jpg/aid15271-v4-728px-Criticize-Constructively-Step-3-Version-7.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If you‚Äôre critiquing a child, you may say, ‚ÄúI love you very much and I appreciate how much work you‚Äôve been putting in at school, but I just got off the phone with your teacher‚Ä¶‚Äù</li> \n    <li>If you‚Äôre talking to an employee, you could say, ‚ÄúI‚Äôve seen you crushing it on the sales calls, and I think you‚Äôre doing a great job, but we need to talk about your punctuality‚Ä¶‚Äù</li> \n    <li>To critique a friend, you might say, ‚ÄúI know you care about me and you know that I care about you, but something has been bugging me recently‚Ä¶‚Äù</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Criticize-Constructively&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6\" title=\"Edit section: Use ‚ÄúI‚Äù statements to keep things positive.\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span id=\"Use-‚ÄúI‚Äù-statements-to-keep-things-positive.\"></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Use-.E2.80.9CI.E2.80.9D-statements-to-keep-things-positive.\">Use ‚ÄúI‚Äù statements to keep things positive.</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Phrase your critique using ‚ÄúI‚Äù to keep them from being defensive. If you come right out and start a bunch of criticisms with ‚Äúyou,‚Äù the other person may feel like you‚Äôre attacking or cornering them. Start with ‚ÄúI‚Äù to frame things around your perspective. This way, it won‚Äôt feel like you‚Äôre trying to impose your beliefs or ideas on them, and they‚Äôll be much more likely to absorb what you‚Äôre getting at.<sup id=\"_ref-5\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 5\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Criticize-Constructively#_note-5\">[5]</a></sup> \n   <ul>\n    <li>For example, instead of saying, ‚ÄúYou need to stop talking to your dad that way,‚Äù you might say, ‚ÄúI don‚Äôt feel good when I hear you talking like that to your father.‚Äù</li> \n    <li>If you were critiquing your friend, you wouldn‚Äôt want to say, ‚ÄúYou never pick up the phone when I call.‚Äù It might be more productive to say, ‚ÄúI feel like we‚Äôre not really talking as often as I‚Äôd like.‚Äù</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Criticize-Constructively&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7\" title=\"Edit section: Give them a chance to self-critique.\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Give-them-a-chance-to-self-critique.\">Give them a chance to self-critique.</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>One way to broach the critique is to let the other person start. You might ask them a hypothetical question about what they might say if you acted the way they have, or encourage them to look at their behavior from a fresh perspective. This is a particularly good idea if you‚Äôre worried about the other person feeling attacked or boxed-in. This may also be a good idea if you aren‚Äôt sure the other person knows if they‚Äôve done anything wrong.<sup id=\"_ref-6\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 6\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Criticize-Constructively#_note-6\">[6]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Criticize-Constructively-Step-5-Version-7.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Criticize Constructively Step 5 Version 7.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/b/b3/Criticize-Constructively-Step-5-Version-7.jpg/aid15271-v4-728px-Criticize-Constructively-Step-5-Version-7.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If your employee has been getting in trouble at work, you could say, ‚ÄúIf you were in charge and you had an employee with multiple customer complaints, how would you address that situation?‚Äù or, ‚ÄúIf you had to evaluate your performance, what would you say?‚Äù</li> \n    <li>If you were talking to your child, you might say, ‚ÄúIf you saw one of your classmates acting like this, what would you think of them?‚Äù</li> \n    <li>If you were talking to a friend, you could ask, ‚ÄúHow do you feel when your friends talk behind your back?‚Äù</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Criticize-Constructively&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8\" title=\"Edit section: Relate the criticism to their goals.\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Relate-the-criticism-to-their-goals.\">Relate the criticism to their goals.</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Emphasizing the benefits of following your feedback will get them on board. If your criticism feels totally disconnected from the other person‚Äôs goals, they won‚Äôt be as receptive to it. Ask yourself, ‚ÄúWhat does this person care about?‚Äù Before (or after) you critique them, explain how the feedback you‚Äôre giving them will help them achieve their goals to get them to buy in.<sup id=\"_ref-7\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 7\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Criticize-Constructively#_note-7\">[7]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Criticize-Constructively-Step-4-Version-7.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Criticize Constructively Step 4 Version 7.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/2/2b/Criticize-Constructively-Step-4-Version-7.jpg/aid15271-v4-728px-Criticize-Constructively-Step-4-Version-7.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If you‚Äôre meeting with an employee that‚Äôs often behind on their work, you might say, ‚ÄúI know you‚Äôre looking for a promotion, so I thought we could chat a bit about things you could change to get where you want to be. How does that sound?‚Äù</li> \n    <li>If a co-worker is underperforming at work, you could say, ‚ÄúI know you‚Äôve mentioned that you‚Äôre trying to improve your sales numbers, and I had an idea that may help with that. Do you want to chat about it?‚Äù</li> \n    <li>If you were talking to a child, you might say, ‚ÄúI know you want to go to summer camp with your friends, but if you don‚Äôt get your grades up, you may end up in summer school.‚Äù</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Criticize-Constructively&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9\" title=\"Edit section: Criticize the behavior, not the person.\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span id=\"Criticize-the-behavior,-not-the-person.\"></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Criticize-the-behavior.2C-not-the-person.\">Criticize the behavior, not the person.</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>It‚Äôs easier for someone to change if they don‚Äôt feel personally attacked. People don‚Äôt always behave in a way that lines up perfectly with who they are or how they see themselves. By focusing strictly on what the other person has done, it‚Äôll be much easier to get them to change. If they feel like you‚Äôre putting them down or challenging who they are as a person, they‚Äôre not going to respond well.<sup id=\"_ref-8\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 8\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Criticize-Constructively#_note-8\">[8]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Criticize-Constructively-Step-6-Version-7.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Criticize Constructively Step 6 Version 7.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/a/ae/Criticize-Constructively-Step-6-Version-7.jpg/aid15271-v4-728px-Criticize-Constructively-Step-6-Version-7.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>For example, instead of telling a struggling salesperson, ‚ÄúYou don‚Äôt have a good rapport with the customers,‚Äù you might say, ‚ÄúI think you could improve the way you communicate with the customers.‚Äù</li> \n    <li>As another example, instead of telling a poorly-dressed co-worker, ‚ÄúYou look sloppy,‚Äù you could say, ‚ÄúI don‚Äôt know if I would choose to wear that to work. Let me explain‚Ä¶‚Äù</li> \n    <li>This is especially important if you‚Äôre critiquing a partner or family member. Don‚Äôt tell your partner, ‚ÄúYou‚Äôre so mean to me!‚Äù say, ‚ÄúI don‚Äôt appreciate it when you talk to me that way.‚Äù</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Criticize-Constructively&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10\" title=\"Edit section: Be honest about how serious the issue is.\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Be-honest-about-how-serious-the-issue-is.\">Be honest about how serious the issue is.</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>If the reason you‚Äôre critiquing them is a big deal, say so. At the same time, if the subject you‚Äôre discussing isn‚Äôt critically important, acknowledge that as well. If someone is just violating a super-minor policy at work and they probably don‚Äôt even know they‚Äôre doing it, don‚Äôt treat it like the end of the world. However, if someone is behaving in a way that‚Äôs jeopardizing someone‚Äôs safety or their job security, it‚Äôs important to drive the point home. Adjust the tone and language based on how essential the criticism is.<sup id=\"_ref-9\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 9\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Criticize-Constructively#_note-9\">[9]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Criticize-Constructively-Step-7-Version-7.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Criticize Constructively Step 7 Version 7.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/c/ca/Criticize-Constructively-Step-7-Version-7.jpg/aid15271-v4-728px-Criticize-Constructively-Step-7-Version-7.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>You might tell an employee who shows up a few minutes late, ‚ÄúLook, I know it seems like a little thing, but I‚Äôd appreciate it if you clock in exactly at 9:00 am, and not 9:04 or 9:02.‚Äù</li> \n    <li>For something serious, like a worker cursing at rude customers, you might say, ‚ÄúI‚Äôve got to level with you here. It‚Äôs extremely important that you don‚Äôt talk to customers like that. It impacts the reputation of this company.‚Äù</li> \n    <li>If you‚Äôre critiquing a child, it‚Äôs important to emphasize why you‚Äôre trying to correct them. If they‚Äôre doing something dangerous, they need to know how serious it is.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Criticize-Constructively&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11\" title=\"Edit section: Acknowledge external circumstances.\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Acknowledge-external-circumstances.\">Acknowledge external circumstances.</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Respecting other factors will help the other person take responsibility. If they‚Äôve been going through a tough time at home, let them know you understand they‚Äôre struggling with some personal stuff. If they acted out because they were being antagonized, admit that you might have behaved the same way but still need to say something. This is key when it comes to getting people to internalize the essence of what you‚Äôre getting at.<sup id=\"_ref-10\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 10\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Criticize-Constructively#_note-10\">[10]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Criticize-Constructively-Step-8-Version-5.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Criticize Constructively Step 8 Version 5.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/4/4f/Criticize-Constructively-Step-8-Version-5.jpg/aid15271-v4-728px-Criticize-Constructively-Step-8-Version-5.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>For example, if you‚Äôre critiquing your partner because they‚Äôre skipping out on housework, you might say, ‚ÄúI know you‚Äôre trying to catch up at work, and I appreciate you for contributing to our home, but I‚Äôd love some help with the dishes every now and then.‚Äù</li> \n    <li>If you‚Äôre talking to a child, you might say, ‚ÄúI know you get excited sometimes and it can be hard to control yourself, but I‚Äôd appreciate it if you don‚Äôt act out like the next time you have friends over.‚Äù</li> \n    <li>You might tell a tired late-night worker, ‚ÄúI know these night shifts are really tough, and it‚Äôs hard to get enough rest, but when I see you sleeping on the job, we have to talk about it.‚Äù</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Criticize-Constructively&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12\" title=\"Edit section: Be concrete about future changes.\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Be-concrete-about-future-changes.\">Be concrete about future changes.</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Give the other person specific steps to take. If your criticism is nebulous or abstract, they‚Äôre going to have a hard time using your criticism in any kind of constructive way. Once you‚Äôve walked through the criticism, provide actionable suggestions that the person might take to improve in the future. You could even offer to help them take those steps!<sup id=\"_ref-11\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 11\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Criticize-Constructively#_note-11\">[11]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Criticize-Constructively-Step-9-Version-5.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Criticize Constructively Step 9 Version 5.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/d/da/Criticize-Constructively-Step-9-Version-5.jpg/aid15271-v4-728px-Criticize-Constructively-Step-9-Version-5.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>For example, you might tell an employee who keeps forgetting a part of their uniform, ‚ÄúSo, the next time you get ready to leave the house for work, remember to check your bag for the name-tag. If you do forget it, come see me before your shift starts and I‚Äôll give you a backup.‚Äù</li> \n    <li>If you have a roommate that's not pulling their weight, you could say, \"Stacy is handling the kitchen and I'm going to clean the bathrooms. Can you take care of the yard work every week?\"</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Criticize-Constructively&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13\" title=\"Edit section: Tell them you believe in them.\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Tell-them-you-believe-in-them.\">Tell them you believe in them.</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>You can lead or close with this, but make them feel supported. If the person being criticized feels like you don‚Äôt believe in them, they‚Äôre going to leave the conversation feeling bad about themselves. If your goal is to help them change for the better, remind them that you appreciate their hard work and know they‚Äôre capable of what you‚Äôre suggesting.<sup id=\"_ref-12\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 12\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Criticize-Constructively#_note-12\">[12]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Criticize-Constructively-Step-10-Version-5.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Criticize Constructively Step 10 Version 5.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/f/f7/Criticize-Constructively-Step-10-Version-5.jpg/aid15271-v4-728px-Criticize-Constructively-Step-10-Version-5.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>For example, you could close out a chat with a struggling student by saying, ‚ÄúI know how smart and kind you are. I believe in you, and I‚Äôm sure you can do this!‚Äù</li> \n    <li>You might tell an employee who‚Äôs struggling with confidence, ‚ÄúYou‚Äôre a real asset to our team, and I know you‚Äôve got what it takes to improve.‚Äù</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Criticize-Constructively&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14\" title=\"Edit section: Respond to concerns with understanding.\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Respond-to-concerns-with-understanding.\">Respond to concerns with understanding.</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Giving the other person a chance to respond is essential. If they don‚Äôt feel like they have a voice, they‚Äôre not going to walk out of the conversation feeling like they‚Äôve been given a fair shake. Give the other person an opportunity to respond or explain how they feel. Even if you think they‚Äôre wrong, or focusing on the wrong part of the criticism, it‚Äôs important for them to feel like you‚Äôre listening.<sup id=\"_ref-13\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 13\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Criticize-Constructively#_note-13\">[13]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Criticize-Constructively-Step-11-Version-5.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Criticize Constructively Step 11 Version 5.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/3/35/Criticize-Constructively-Step-11-Version-5.jpg/aid15271-v4-728px-Criticize-Constructively-Step-11-Version-5.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>You could close out with something like, ‚ÄúDoes all of this sound fair to you?‚Äù or, ‚ÄúHow do you feel about all of this?‚Äù and just let the other person share.</li> \n    <li>If they seem resistant by the end of the conversation, you could even close with something like, ‚ÄúI totally get why you‚Äôre frustrated. I‚Äôd be frustrated too, but we still need to address this.‚Äù</li> \n    <li>If they get defensive or upset that you‚Äôre critiquing them, try to reel things in a bit and remind them you‚Äôre just trying to help. You might say, ‚ÄúI‚Äôm not trying to put you down here. I‚Äôm just trying to help, and I‚Äôm sorry if it doesn‚Äôt feel that way.‚Äù</li> \n    <li>If someone gets so bent out of shape that they start yelling or something, keep calm, try to help them relax, and just let it go. They‚Äôre clearly not in a headspace where this is going to be a productive conversation.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Criticize-Constructively&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15\" title=\"Edit section: Tips\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Tips\">Tips</span></h2> \n <ul>\n  <li>The ‚Äúfeedback sandwich‚Äù is solid if you aren‚Äôt critiquing someone at work, but in an office setting, many professionals will spot this maneuver right away because it‚Äôs so popular. This may have an unintended consequence of making your criticism feel insincere.<sup id=\"_ref-14\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 14\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Criticize-Constructively#_note-14\">[14]</a></sup></li>\n </ul> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Criticize-Constructively&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16\" title=\"Edit section: Related wikiHows\">Edit</a><span
