images/thumb/c/ca/Criticize-Constructively-Step-7-Version-7.jpg/aid15271-v4-728px-Criticize-Constructively-Step-7-Version-7.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn89@2020_2/2021/04/07/17-38-38-224_288cfaf47a71e9ba.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/4/4f/Criticize-Constructively-Step-8-Version-5.jpg/aid15271-v4-728px-Criticize-Constructively-Step-8-Version-5.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn52@2020_1/2021/04/07/17-38-23-823_1ad0325d5e3ea81b.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/d/da/Criticize-Constructively-Step-9-Version-5.jpg/aid15271-v4-728px-Criticize-Constructively-Step-9-Version-5.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn35@2020_4/2021/04/07/17-38-23-935_7dd3e483461a12d9.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/f/f7/Criticize-Constructively-Step-10-Version-5.jpg/aid15271-v4-728px-Criticize-Constructively-Step-10-Version-5.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn82@2020_4/2021/04/07/17-38-24-687_1cd3c705666a68db.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/3/35/Criticize-Constructively-Step-11-Version-5.jpg/aid15271-v4-728px-Criticize-Constructively-Step-11-Version-5.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn92@2020_1/2021/04/07/17-38-23-733_104ab01454a550f2.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1617817069929},{"createdTime":"2021-04-08 01:37:49","updatedTime":"2021-04-08 01:37:49","title":"How to Address a Letter to a Family","link":"https://www.wikihow.com/Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family","description":"<div class=\"mw-parser-output\">\n <p>If you're writing a letter to a family, there are several ways you can address them. Most letters start off with \"Dear\" and then the person or family's name. For a casual and friendly salutation, list each of their first names, while a more formal letter could address a family using titles like \"Ms.\" or Mr.\" For a simple solution, address the family as a collective group by writing their last name and then \"family\" after it. </p> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1\" title=\"Edit section: Steps\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Steps\">Steps</span></h2> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2\" title=\"Edit section: Choosing the Correct Written Name\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Choosing-the-Correct-Written-Name\">Choosing the Correct Written Name</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Start your letter with the salutation ‚ÄúDear.‚Äù This is the most common way to begin a letter to someone. Write ‚ÄúDear‚Äù and then the person‚Äôs name or family‚Äôs names right after it.<sup id=\"_ref-1\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 1\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family#_note-1\">[1]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-1.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Address a Letter to a Family Step 1.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/e/e7/Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-1.jpg/aid11385411-v4-728px-Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-1.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Instead of ‚ÄúDear,‚Äù you might choose to begin the letter with ‚ÄúHello.‚Äù</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Call the family members by their first names for a casual greeting. This is a good way to begin your letter if you know the family well. After ‚ÄúDear,‚Äù write each person‚Äôs name starting with the parents and ending with the children‚Äôs names.<sup id=\"_ref-2\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 2\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family#_note-2\">[2]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Address a Letter to a Family Step 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/e/e9/Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-2.jpg/aid11385411-v4-728px-Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>For a more personal touch, consider adding the family‚Äôs pet names onto the list at the end as well.</li> \n    <li>Tack on the family‚Äôs last name after the last person‚Äôs first name, if desired. For example: ‚ÄúDear Sally, David, and Lilly Stevens.‚Äù</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Address the family as a collective group by writing their last name and ‚ÄúFamily.‚Äù For example, ‚ÄúDear Smith family,‚Äù or ‚ÄúTo the Turner Family.‚Äù This eliminates the need to write each person‚Äôs name and is a great condensed salutation.<sup id=\"_ref-3\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 3\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family#_note-3\">[3]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-3.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Address a Letter to a Family Step 3.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/4/48/Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-3.jpg/aid11385411-v4-728px-Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-3.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Whether you choose to capitalize the word ‚Äúfamily‚Äù is up to you, but the family‚Äôs last name should always be capitalized.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Add \"Mr\" and \"Mrs\" to make your writing more formal. These titles can be tacked on before first names or last names. For instance, your letter might start off with, ‚ÄúDear Mr. and Mrs. Adams,‚Äù or ‚ÄúDear Ms. Kate, Mr. Robert, and Miss Sierra.‚Äù This makes your letter a bit more official and proper.<sup id=\"_ref-4\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 4\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family#_note-4\">[4]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-4.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Address a Letter to a Family Step 4.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/8/89/Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-4.jpg/aid11385411-v4-728px-Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-4.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If you‚Äôre not sure how a woman prefers to be addressed, use ‚ÄúMs.‚Äù</li> \n    <li>Another example might be, ‚ÄúDear Ms. Stern and Mr. Lichtman.‚Äù</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Write each person‚Äôs individual name if they don‚Äôt share the same last name. This is used if you‚Äôre addressing a married couple that uses different last names, as well as an unmarried couple or children that live in the same house but share different last names. Either write their first and last names, or write each person‚Äôs last name with a title in front of it.<sup id=\"_ref-5\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 5\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family#_note-5\">[5]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-5.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Address a Letter to a Family Step 5.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/5/51/Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-5.jpg/aid11385411-v4-728px-Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-5.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>For example, you might write, ‚ÄúDear Ross Green and Trudy Smith.‚Äù</li> \n    <li>Another example would be, ‚ÄúDear Mr. Thornhill and Mrs. Morgan.‚Äù</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Use a distinguishing title if a person in the family has one. If an adult in the family is a doctor, reverend, or other type of distinguished person, add their title before their name. For example, if you‚Äôre addressing a doctor, you would write, ‚ÄúDear Dr. Parker‚Äù along with the rest of the family's names.<sup id=\"_ref-6\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 6\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family#_note-6\">[6]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-6.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Address a Letter to a Family Step 6.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/f/f7/Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-6.jpg/aid11385411-v4-728px-Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-6.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Add the titles for military personnel and judges as well.</li> \n    <li>Another example would be, ‚ÄúDear Lieutenant Allen and family,‚Äù or ‚ÄúDear. Reverend Smith, Mrs. Smith, and family.‚Äù</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Add a comma after the name and begin writing your letter. Once you‚Äôve written the family‚Äôs name as you‚Äôd like it to appear in your letter, add a comma as punctuation for the salutation. Skip a line or two after writing the salutation, and begin writing the body of your letter.<sup id=\"_ref-7\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 7\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family#_note-7\">[7]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-7.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Address a Letter to a Family Step 7.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/c/c3/Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-7.jpg/aid11385411-v4-728px-Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-7.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Instead of a comma, you could also use a colon or em dash, though a comma is most common.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3\" title=\"Edit section: Addressing the Envelope\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Addressing-the-Envelope\">Addressing the Envelope</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Use neat handwriting to make sure the post office can read the address. It‚Äôs best to print the names and address instead of writing them in cursive to ensure that they‚Äôre legible. Use neat handwriting and a pen so your letter gets to the right place.<sup id=\"_ref-8\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 8\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family#_note-8\">[8]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-8.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Address a Letter to a Family Step 8.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/b/b4/Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-8.jpg/aid11385411-v4-728px-Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-8.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div></li> \n  <li>Write the return address in the top left corner of the envelope. This is the sender‚Äôs address, so if you‚Äôre writing the letter, you‚Äôll put your address in the top left corner. Write your full name on the first line, your street address or PO box on the second line, and your city, state, and zip code on the third line.<sup id=\"_ref-9\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 9\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family#_note-9\">[9]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-9.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Address a Letter to a Family Step 9.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/a/a4/Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-9.jpg/aid11385411-v4-728px-Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-9.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Start your writing in the uppermost corner to ensure you have enough space.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Put the family name and address in the center of the envelope. Since you don‚Äôt have a lot of space in the middle of the envelope, avoid listing each family member‚Äôs name and instead just write their collective family last name. Write the family name in the center of the envelope, their street address right below their name, and their city, state, and zip code on the third line.<sup id=\"_ref-10\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 10\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family#_note-10\">[10]</a></sup><sup id=\"_ref-11\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 11\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family#_note-11\">[11]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-10.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Address a Letter to a Family Step 10.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/e/ea/Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-10.jpg/aid11385411-v4-728px-Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-10.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If the family contains people with different last names, you might address the envelope as, ‚ÄúThe Smiths and the Walkers.‚Äù</li> \n    <li>Use the family‚Äôs PO box if they don‚Äôt have a street address.</li> \n    <li>A sample envelope might read (first line) The Jones Family (second line) 1234 wikiHow Place (third line) Palo Alto, California 94301.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Place a stamp in the top right corner so your letter is ready to be mailed. Use enough postage to ensure your letter gets to its destination. Place the stamp (or multiple stamps) in the upper right corner, pressing down on it to make sure it sticks.<sup id=\"_ref-12\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 12\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family#_note-12\">[12]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-11.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Address a Letter to a Family Step 11.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/5/50/Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-11.jpg/aid11385411-v4-728px-Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-11.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If you‚Äôre not sure how many stamps to use, go online to the post office‚Äôs website for more information.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n \n</div>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Tue, 06 Apr 2021 00:00:00 +0000","feedId":44,"bgimg":"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/e/e7/Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-1.jpg/aid11385411-v4-728px-Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-1.jpg","linkMd5":"1397be0bcf965eeff0cf9f190e0ffdc7","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn7@2020_3/2021/04/07/17-37-53-733_b3c160debf44fb0f.webp","destWidth":728,"destHeight":546,"sourceBytes":23203,"destBytes":7626,"author":"","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/e/e7/Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-1.jpg/aid11385411-v4-728px-Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-1.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn7@2020_3/2021/04/07/17-37-53-733_b3c160debf44fb0f.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/e/e9/Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-2.jpg/aid11385411-v4-728px-Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-2.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn76@2020_6/2021/04/07/17-38-24-479_56369ad3e9758204.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/4/48/Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-3.jpg/aid11385411-v4-728px-Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-3.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn3@2020_1/2021/04/07/17-38-25-190_6f94465919ca017c.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/8/89/Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-4.jpg/aid11385411-v4-728px-Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-4.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn84@2020_5/2021/04/07/17-38-23-605_13a60ec53dc5a376.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/5/51/Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-5.jpg/aid11385411-v4-728px-Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-5.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn40@2020_6/2021/04/07/17-38-24-968_90e1dfbe2a01fcf0.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/f/f7/Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-6.jpg/aid11385411-v4-728px-Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-6.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn19@2020_3/2021/04/07/17-38-25-057_708a6050e16f7798.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/c/c3/Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-7.jpg/aid11385411-v4-728px-Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-7.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn98@2020_2/2021/04/07/17-38-24-979_83fc70dd6997ecc5.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/b/b4/Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-8.jpg/aid11385411-v4-728px-Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-8.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn76@2020_6/2021/04/07/17-38-25-199_810836bc05ae0107.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/a/a4/Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-9.jpg/aid11385411-v4-728px-Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-9.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn39@2020_3/2021/04/07/17-38-23-661_2b5a7ee4b4fc8304.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/e/ea/Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-10.jpg/aid11385411-v4-728px-Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-10.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn31@2020_6/2021/04/07/17-38-24-339_41012d6c0f5f9f32.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/5/50/Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-11.jpg/aid11385411-v4-728px-Address-a-Letter-to-a-Family-Step-11.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn19@2020_1/2021/04/07/17-38-23-756_9c8bdd18f200df05.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1617817069925},{"createdTime":"2021-04-08 01:37:49","updatedTime":"2021-04-08 01:37:49","title":"How to Remove a Hot Sauce Stain","link":"https://www.wikihow.com/Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain","description":"<div class=\"mw-parser-output\">\n <p>If you love the spicy thrill of putting hot sauce on everything, chances are you've had to deal with a spill or two. The oils and red pigment from the chili peppers in hot sauce can turn a small splatter into a stubborn stain, but don't give up hope! Whether you need to clean hot sauce from your clothing, carpet, or countertops, these solutions might just do the trick. </p> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1\" title=\"Edit section: Steps\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Steps\">Steps</span></h2> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2\" title=\"Edit section: Cleaning Hot Sauce Stains out of Clothing\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Cleaning-Hot-Sauce-Stains-out-of-Clothing\">Cleaning Hot Sauce Stains out of Clothing</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Scrape off any excess hot sauce as soon as possible. Try using a spoon, butter knife, credit card, or even a paper towel to rub away as much of the hot sauce as you can. The stain will be easiest to treat if you get to it right away, but even if it dries before you notice it, start treating it as soon as you're able to.<sup id=\"_ref-1\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 1\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain#_note-1\">[1]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain-Step-1.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Remove a Hot Sauce Stain Step 1.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/0/03/Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain-Step-1.jpg/aid11643066-v4-728px-Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain-Step-1.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>The more hot sauce that's present, the more likely the stain will be to spread once you start trying to clean it, which is why scraping off the excess is important.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Coat large, fresh stains with baking powder, then rinse with cool water. To absorb some of the oil from the stain, sprinkle a generous layer of baking powder over the entire surface of the stain. Leave it in place for at least 15 minutes, then turn the garment inside-out and rinse the back of the stain with cold running water.<sup id=\"_ref-2\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 2\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain#_note-2\">[2]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain-Step-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Remove a Hot Sauce Stain Step 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/5/57/Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain-Step-2.jpg/aid11643066-v4-728px-Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain-Step-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>While this isn't likely to take the stain out of the garment, it can make it easier to clean, since it helps remove some of the oil.</li> \n    <li>You can also use cornstarch if you don't have any baking powder on hand.</li> \n    <li>Rinsing the stain from the back will help flush the oil out of the fabric without spreading the stain.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Rub liquid laundry detergent out of the stain and let it sit for 3-5 minutes. Pour a small amount of liquid laundry detergent onto the garment, then gently rub the detergent onto the surface of the stain. Wait for about 3-5 minutes, then turn the garment inside-out and rinse the spot under cold running water. When you're finished, launder the garment as usual.<sup id=\"_ref-3\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 3\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain#_note-3\">[3]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain-Step-3.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Remove a Hot Sauce Stain Step 3.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/f/fd/Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain-Step-3.jpg/aid11643066-v4-728px-Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain-Step-3.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Do not use bar soap or powder detergent. You'll likely have to scrub to get these to cover the spot, which could set the stain deeper into the fabric.</li> \n    <li>This is especially useful for cleaning a stain that's dried, although it will work on fresh hot sauce stains, as well.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Clean the spot with rubbing alcohol for a quick fix. If you want to lighten a hot sauce stain quickly, blot the area with rubbing alcohol and clean paper towels. Continue blotting until most of the stain is gone. Your garment should dry quickly once you're finished!<sup id=\"_ref-4\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 4\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain#_note-4\">[4]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain-Step-4.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Remove a Hot Sauce Stain Step 4.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/d/d7/Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain-Step-4.jpg/aid11643066-v4-728px-Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain-Step-4.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>You can also use hand sanitizer or white vinegar if you don't have rubbing alcohol available. Just make sure the hand sanitizer is clear and fragrance-free so it won't stain your clothes.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Wash the garment as usual once you lighten the stain. No matter which stain removal method you use, once you get the majority of the hot sauce out of the garment, run the clothing through your washing machine on a cool cycle. Examine the garment closely once you finish washing it. If the hot sauce is completely gone, put the clothing in the dryer or hang it up to dry. If there's still a faint stain, continue treating the garment until it's gone.\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain-Step-5.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Remove a Hot Sauce Stain Step 5.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/0/0a/Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain-Step-5.jpg/aid11643066-v4-728px-Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain-Step-5.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Washing the garment in cool water will prevent the stain from setting into the fabric if it isn't completely gone.</li> \n    <li>If you prefer, you can hand wash the garment instead.</li> \n    <li>Drying the clothing can set in the stain, which is why it's important to check before you put it in the dryer.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3\" title=\"Edit section: Getting the Stain out of Carpet or Upholstery\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Getting-the-Stain-out-of-Carpet-or-Upholstery\">Getting the Stain out of Carpet or Upholstery</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Blot up or scrape off any excess hot sauce. If you spilled hot sauce in your carpet or splattered it on your couch, try to remove as much of the stain as you can. To do that, blot the area with a clean, dry cloth if the stain is fresh, or scrape off any dried hot sauce with a butter knife, spoon, or paper towel.<sup id=\"_ref-5\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 5\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain#_note-5\">[5]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain-Step-6.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Remove a Hot Sauce Stain Step 6.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/1/1e/Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain-Step-6.jpg/aid11643066-v4-728px-Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain-Step-6.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>This will help keep the stain from getting larger when you add your cleaner.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Mix of water and of liquid soap. In a small bowl or shallow container, mix cool, clean water with a small amount of liquid dish soap. Then, stir the mixture gently with a spoon or your hand so it's thoroughly combined.<sup id=\"_ref-6\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 6\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain#_note-6\">[6]</a></sup> of white vinegar to the mixture.}}\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain-Step-7.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Remove a Hot Sauce Stain Step 7.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/a/a2/Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain-Step-7.jpg/aid11643066-v4-728px-Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain-Step-7.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If you use warm water, the stain could set deeper into the fabric.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Dampen a white cloth with the mixture and wring out the excess. Take a clean, white cloth and dip it in the soapy water you just mixed up. Then, wring out the cloth until it stops dripping.<sup id=\"_ref-7\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 7\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain#_note-7\">[7]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain-Step-8.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Remove a Hot Sauce Stain Step 8.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/9/9c/Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain-Step-8.jpg/aid11643066-v4-728px-Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain-Step-8.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>In general, when you're cleaning carpet or upholstery, it's best to use as little water as possible to avoid spreading the stain or leaving water spots.</li> \n    <li>Using a white cloth will ensure that you don't transfer any dye from the towel to the upholstery.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Dab the stain with the wet cloth from the outside in. Blot the outside edges of the stain first, working in toward the center. Continue patting the stain, switching to a clean portion of the cloth as needed until the spot is gone. You can also dip the cloth in the soapy water and wring it out again if it starts to dry out.<sup id=\"_ref-8\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 8\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain#_note-8\">[8]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain-Step-9.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Remove a Hot Sauce Stain Step 9.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/7/78/Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain-Step-9.jpg/aid11643066-v4-728px-Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain-Step-9.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>To keep up with what side of the cloth you've already used, try folding it into quarters before you start. Work on the first side, then flip the cloth over and use the second side once that's dirty. Then, turn the last fold inside-out and you'll have 2 clean sections of the cloth to work with.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Blot the area with cold water and a clean cloth to remove the soap. Once you've gotten the stain out of the carpet or upholstery, pour out your soapy water and replace it with clean, cold water. Dip a clean, white cloth in the cold water and wring it out, then blot away any soapy residue that's left behind.<sup id=\"_ref-9\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 9\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain#_note-9\">[9]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain-Step-10.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Remove a Hot Sauce Stain Step 10.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/1/17/Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain-Step-10.jpg/aid11643066-v4-728px-Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain-Step-10.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Over time, the soap will lead to a large dirty-looking stain if you don't remove it.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Dry the area with a clean cloth. After you blot up the soap, take a clean, dry towel and pat the area dry, absorbing as much of the water as possible. If any dampness remains, let the spot air dry overnight.<sup id=\"_ref-10\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 10\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain#_note-10\">[10]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain-Step-11.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Remove a Hot Sauce Stain Step 11.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/d/d8/Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain-Step-11.jpg/aid11643066-v4-728px-Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain-Step-11.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>The cloth you use to dry the area should be white as well. Colored towels may leave behind residual dye that could stain your carpet or upholstery.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4\" title=\"Edit section: Treating Hard Surfaces\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Treating-Hard-Surfaces\">Treating Hard Surfaces</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Soak plastic containers in rubbing alcohol to remove hot sauce stains. If the stains are on the inside of a container, fill the container with enough rubbing alcohol to completely cover the stained area. If the stain is on the outside, fill a larger container with the rubbing alcohol, then submerge the smaller container in the alcohol. Let it sit overnight, then rinse thoroughly with cold water.<sup id=\"_ref-11\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 11\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain#_note-11\">[11]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain-Step-12.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Remove a Hot Sauce Stain Step 12.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/8/89/Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain-Step-12.jpg/aid11643066-v4-728px-Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain-Step-12.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>You can also use hand sanitizer, bleach that's diluted 1:10 with water, or white vinegar.<sup id=\"_ref-12\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 12\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain#_note-12\">[12]</a></sup></li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Cover small plastic items with lemon juice and put them in the sun. To bleach hot sauce stains off of dishes, toys, or other small items, rub lemon juice over the stain. Then, put it outside on a sunny day for 1-2 hours. The stain should be noticeably lighter, and it may even disappear entirely.<sup id=\"_ref-13\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 13\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain#_note-13\">[13]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain-Step-13.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Remove a Hot Sauce Stain Step 13.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/1/1e/Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain-Step-13.jpg/aid11643066-v4-728px-Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain-Step-13.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Lemon juice alone may lighten the stain, although it's more effective in combination with the sunlight.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Apply baking soda paste to remove hot sauce from countertops. If you spilled hot sauce on your counter and it stained, try mixing baking soda with just enough water to make a thick, grainy paste. Spread the paste over the entire surface of the stain and let it sit for at least 30 minutes, although for stubborn stains, you may want to leave the paste on overnight. Then, rinse the area with cool water.<sup id=\"_ref-14\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 14\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain#_note-14\">[14]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain-Step-14.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Remove a Hot Sauce Stain Step 14.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/b/ba/Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain-Step-14.jpg/aid11643066-v4-728px-Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain-Step-14.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>You can also try using the baking soda paste as a scrub to clean hot sauce stains.</li> \n    <li>A paste made of denture tablets or effervescent antacids may be effective, as well.<sup id=\"_ref-15\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 15\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain#_note-15\">[15]</a></sup></li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Use table salt to scrub stains from smooth surfaces. Pour salt over the surface of the stain. Then, take a damp cloth and rub it into the salt in a circular motion. The abrasiveness of the salt scrub should help work the stain out of the surface.<sup id=\"_ref-16\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 16\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain#_note-16\">[16]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain-Step-15.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Remove a Hot Sauce Stain Step 15.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/7/73/Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain-Step-15.jpg/aid11643066-v4-728px-Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain-Step-15.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>For instance, you can use this to scrub countertops, tabletops, or dishes with stubborn hot sauce stains.</li> \n    <li>Because this scrub is abrasive, avoid using it on any surface that would be easily scratched, like marble or lacquered surfaces.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Remove-a-Hot-Sauce-Stain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5\" title=\"Edit section: ebp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1617817069925},{"createdTime":"2021-04-08 01:37:49","updatedTime":"2021-04-08 01:37:49","title":"How to Develop Productive Habits","link":"https://www.wikihow.com/Develop-Productive-Habits","description":"<div class=\"mw-parser-output\">\n <p>It can be kind of challenging to force yourself to start a bunch of productive habits out of nowhere. Luckily, with a few minor changes to your environment and workflow, anyone can set the stage for success. All it takes is a little bit of preparation and a healthy dose of positive thinking to become the most productive version of yourself. With the right attitude and a little effort, you'll be crossing tasks off of your to-do list faster than you can write them out! </p> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Develop-Productive-Habits&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1\" title=\"Edit section: Steps\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Steps\">Steps</span></h2> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Develop-Productive-Habits&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2\" title=\"Edit section: Use a daily planner.\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Use-a-daily-planner.\">Use a daily planner.</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Mapping your day out will keep you focus on what‚Äôs important. Being productive has more to do with organization than effort, so put 5-10 minutes aside every night (or morning) to map out how you‚Äôre going to spend the day ahead of you.<sup id=\"_ref-1\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 1\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Develop-Productive-Habits#_note-1\">[1]</a></sup> Fill in the morning with your most time-sensitive or important tasks and set aside time for emails, organization, and breaks.<sup id=\"_ref-2\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 2\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Develop-Productive-Habits#_note-2\">[2]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Develop-Productive-Habits-Step-1-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Develop Productive Habits Step 1 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/c/c0/Develop-Productive-Habits-Step-1-Version-2.jpg/aid7105933-v4-728px-Develop-Productive-Habits-Step-1-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Set concrete goals for each day. Choose 3 important tasks that you want to accomplish and reserve at least 90 minutes to tackle these goals.<sup id=\"_ref-3\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 3\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Develop-Productive-Habits#_note-3\">[3]</a></sup></li> \n    <li>If you want to build your daily schedule in the morning, get up 5-10 minutes earlier than you normally would to make time for it. Productive days don‚Äôt start with a rushed morning schedule!</li> \n    <li>Break the day down into sections so that you don‚Äôt spend hours in the same place or doing the same thing. Moving around regularly and mixing things up will make it easier to sustain focus throughout the day.<sup id=\"_ref-4\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 4\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Develop-Productive-Habits#_note-4\">[4]</a></sup></li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Develop-Productive-Habits&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3\" title=\"Edit section: Stay off of your phone.\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Stay-off-of-your-phone.\">Stay off of your phone.</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Unless you‚Äôre waiting on an important call, keep your phone on silent. It‚Äôs super easy to get distracted by random texts, notifications, and social media. If you catch yourself procrastinating on the phone, stop.<sup id=\"_ref-5\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 5\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Develop-Productive-Habits#_note-5\">[5]</a></sup> You‚Äôre most productive when you‚Äôre focused and engaged in what you‚Äôre trying to accomplish, so minimizing the most obvious distractions is essential.<sup id=\"_ref-6\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 6\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Develop-Productive-Habits#_note-6\">[6]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Develop-Productive-Habits-Step-2-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Develop Productive Habits Step 2 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/7/7a/Develop-Productive-Habits-Step-2-Version-2.jpg/aid7105933-v4-728px-Develop-Productive-Habits-Step-2-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If you‚Äôre compulsively checking social media, there are apps you can download to lock you out of your account part of the day or after you‚Äôve been scrolling for a while.</li> \n    <li>You can always leave your phone in another room or in a desk drawer if you really want to zero in on something.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Develop-Productive-Habits&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4\" title=\"Edit section: Declutter your home or workspace.\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Declutter-your-home-or-workspace.\">Declutter your home or workspace.</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>A clean desk and organized home will help you stay focused. Chaos has a way of drawing your attention away from whatever task you‚Äôre trying to complete.<sup id=\"_ref-7\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 7\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Develop-Productive-Habits#_note-7\">[7]</a></sup> At the end of each day, spend a few minutes throwing out trash, putting things away, and organizing your workspace or home to get rid of clutter. If you wake up to a clean home or show up at work to a minimalist desk, it‚Äôll be easier to build healthy habits.<sup id=\"_ref-8\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 8\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Develop-Productive-Habits#_note-8\">[8]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Develop-Productive-Habits-Step-3-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Develop Productive Habits Step 3 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/6/67/Develop-Productive-Habits-Step-3-Version-2.jpg/aid7105933-v4-728px-Develop-Productive-Habits-Step-3-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>The phrase ‚Äúout of sight, out of mind‚Äù works the other way as well. People tend to be attracted to whatever is in front of them. If there‚Äôs a stack of important files you need to address sitting on your desk, keep them out and take everything else off of your desk.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Develop-Productive-Habits&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5\" title=\"Edit section: Complete important tasks before lunch.\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Complete-important-tasks-before-lunch.\">Complete important tasks before lunch.</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Most people are more productive in the morning, so do key tasks early. If your goal for the day is to go grocery shopping, don‚Äôt put it off until 8 pm when you‚Äôre likely to be tired. If you want to pitch a new service to a few important clients, make those calls or schedule those meetings before noon. This way, you won‚Äôt have to fight off any afternoon sluggishness when you‚Äôre trying to get stuff done.<sup id=\"_ref-9\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 9\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Develop-Productive-Habits#_note-9\">[9]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Develop-Productive-Habits-Step-4-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Develop Productive Habits Step 4 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/1/1d/Develop-Productive-Habits-Step-4-Version-2.jpg/aid7105933-v4-728px-Develop-Productive-Habits-Step-4-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Not only will you get the most important stuff done by scheduling your day this way, but that early feeling of accomplishment will help you maintain momentum throughout the day.</li> \n    <li>If you‚Äôre struggling to maintain your energy later in the day and you aren‚Äôt at work, take a short rest. A 20-minute nap is a great way to put yourself back into a productive headspace.<sup id=\"_ref-10\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 10\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Develop-Productive-Habits#_note-10\">[10]</a></sup></li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Develop-Productive-Habits&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6\" title=\"Edit section: Focus on one thing at a time.\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Focus-on-one-thing-at-a-time.\">Focus on one thing at a time.</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Multi-tasking is rarely a productive way to go about things. You‚Äôre more likely to get things done if you dedicate all of your energy to a single task at a time. Turn the radio off at work, shut the TV off while you study, and don‚Äôt split your time between answering emails and other work-related tasks.<sup id=\"_ref-11\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 11\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Develop-Productive-Habits#_note-11\">[11]</a></sup> When you switch back and forth between different activities, you lose a lot of energy as your brain recalibrates for the new task. This kind of juggling is not a healthy habit for productivity.<sup id=\"_ref-12\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 12\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Develop-Productive-Habits#_note-12\">[12]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Develop-Productive-Habits-Step-5-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Develop Productive Habits Step 5 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/a/ad/Develop-Productive-Habits-Step-5-Version-2.jpg/aid7105933-v4-728px-Develop-Productive-Habits-Step-5-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>You‚Äôre most productive when you‚Äôre in that flow where time is flying and you‚Äôre just totally consumed with what you‚Äôre doing. It‚Äôs a lot harder to get into that state if you‚Äôre constantly jumping between 2-3 different things.<sup id=\"_ref-13\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 13\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Develop-Productive-Habits#_note-13\">[13]</a></sup></li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Develop-Productive-Habits&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7\" title=\"Edit section: Find the value in the boring stuff.\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Find-the-value-in-the-boring-stuff.\">Find the value in the boring stuff.</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>It‚Äôs hard to be productive if you think you‚Äôre doing something pointless. Start pushing yourself to find the significance in every single thing you do before you start. For example, if you‚Äôre just filling out a timesheet for work, remind yourself that you‚Äôre helping your company keep you accountable. In turn, this helps you stay productive at work, and you want to be productive! You can even tie all of that back to your company‚Äôs mission and remind yourself why that‚Äôs important as well.<sup id=\"_ref-14\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 14\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Develop-Productive-Habits#_note-14\">[14]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Develop-Productive-Habits-Step-6-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Develop Productive Habits Step 6 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/a/a3/Develop-Productive-Habits-Step-6-Version-2.jpg/aid7105933-v4-728px-Develop-Productive-Habits-Step-6-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Finding value in the little stuff also improves your overall attitude. If you walk around all day feeling like you‚Äôre wasting your time, you‚Äôre never going to get anything done!</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Develop-Productive-Habits&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8\" title=\"Edit section: Take a short break every hour.\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Take-a-short-break-every-hour.\">Take a short break every hour.</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Set aside 5-10 minutes to recharge your batteries every hour. Stand up and stretch, step outside for a breath of fresh air, or walk around the hallway for a few minutes. Aside from the fact that this will help you come back to the task at hand feeling recharged, it will also give your body a break from sitting or staring at a screen for too long depending on what you‚Äôve been doing.<sup id=\"_ref-15\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 15\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Develop-Productive-Habits#_note-15\">[15]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Develop-Productive-Habits-Step-7-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Develop Productive Habits Step 7 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/4/49/Develop-Productive-Habits-Step-7-Version-2.jpg/aid7105933-v4-728px-Develop-Productive-Habits-Step-7-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Many productive folks are a big fan of the Pomodoro technique. This is where you work in a series of intense bursts by spending 25 minutes focusing on a task and then taking 5 minutes off. This can be a great option if you find yourself losing momentum after every 35-45 minutes or so.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Develop-Productive-Habits&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9\" title=\"Edit section: Make a daily 5-minute investment.\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Make-a-daily-5-minute-investment.\">Make a daily 5-minute investment.</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Start small and let tiny behaviors snowball into regular habits. Force yourself to spend just 5 minutes a day on a new behavior. Next week, double it. For the next week or two, stick to that 10-minutes-a-day rule. After a few weeks, your brain will be so used to spending 10 minutes on this task that it‚Äôll become a habit. This is a phenomenal way to get yourself to build small procedural habits, like working out in the morning, or meditating every afternoon.<sup id=\"_ref-16\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 16\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Develop-Productive-Habits#_note-16\">[16]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Develop-Productive-Habits-Step-8-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Develop Productive Habits Step 8 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/2/22/Develop-Productive-Habits-Step-8-Version-2.jpg/aid7105933-v4-728px-Develop-Productive-Habits-Step-8-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>It may be hard to push through that first week if you aren‚Äôt used to doing something, but stick with it! It will only get easier over time.</li> \n    <li>Completing your tiny habit at the same time every day will also help turn your behavior into a habit.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Develop-Productive-Habits&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10\" title=\"Edit section: Relax on your days off.\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Relax-on-your-days-off.\">Relax on your days off.</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>If you never take some time off, you‚Äôre going to burn yourself out. Make sure that you set aside time to hang out with your friends and family, catch up on that book you‚Äôve been meaning to read, and do things that you actively enjoy. If you‚Äôre constantly pushing yourself to accomplish task after task, you‚Äôre going to run yourself into the ground. Chilling out on your days off is important if you‚Äôre going to be productive!<sup id=\"_ref-17\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 17\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Develop-Productive-Habits#_note-17\">[17]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Develop-Productive-Habits-Step-9-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Develop Productive Habits Step 9 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/0/03/Develop-Productive-Habits-Step-9-Version-2.jpg/aid7105933-v4-728px-Develop-Productive-Habits-Step-9-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If you‚Äôre going to try and implement a new system or habit, take a vacation or long weekend off to get some relaxation in. There‚Äôs some evidence that it‚Äôs easier to build a new habit after a prolonged period of relaxation.<sup id=\"_ref-18\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 18\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Develop-Productive-Habits#_note-18\">[18]</a></sup></li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Develop-Productive-Habits&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11\" title=\"Edit section: Take care of your body.\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Take-care-of-your-body.\">Take care of your body.</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Eat a healthy diet, keep a regular sleep schedule, and exercise regularly. Do your best to stick to a balanced diet full of lean protein, vegetables, and whole grains. Aim to get 8 hours of sleep every night and try to go to bed and wake up at the same time every day.<sup id=\"_ref-19\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 19\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Develop-Productive-Habits#_note-19\">[19]</a></sup> Try to get at least 150 minutes of exercise a week in the form of running, biking, or weightlifting to relieve stress and feel great about yourself!<sup id=\"_ref-20\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 20\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Develop-Productive-Habits#_note-20\">[20]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Develop-Productive-Habits-Step-10.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Develop Productive Habits Step 10.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/5/5c/Develop-Productive-Habits-Step-10.jpg/aid7105933-v4-728px-Develop-Productive-Habits-Step-10.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>It‚Äôs impossible to build productive habits if you don‚Äôt feel good. Taking care of your body is important for your overall health, but it‚Äôs also extremely key if you want to be a productive person.</li> \n    <li>Take care of your mind and soul as well! Meditation and yoga are great ways to stay mentally and emotionally healthy.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Develop-Productive-Habits&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12\" title=\"Edit section: Reward yourself for building productive habits.\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Reward-yourself-for-building-productive-habits.\">Reward yourself for building productive habits.</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>As you‚Äôre improving your overall productivity, reward yourself for sticking with it. After you fill out your planner for the day, take a minute or two to enjoy a warm cup of coffee. Once you finish filing those reports in the morning, eat a small piece of candy. Giving yourself regular, small rewards for sticking with your productive habits is essential to making those habits permanent.<sup id=\"_ref-21\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 21\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Develop-Productive-Habits#_note-21\">[21]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Develop-Productive-Habits-Step-11.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Develop Productive Habits Step 11.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/5/5b/Develop-Productive-Habits-Step-11.jpg/aid7105933-v4-728px-Develop-Productive-Habits-Step-11.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Time your breaks so that you take them right after you‚Äôve finished a productive task. Breaks are a great way to reward yourself and you need to take regular breaks anyway. That‚Äôs a win-win!</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Develop-Productive-Habits&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13\" title=\"Edit section: Video\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Video\">Video</span></h2> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Develop-Productive-Habits&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14\" title=\"Edit section: Tips\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Tips\">Tips</span></h2> \n <ul>\n  <li>It can take a few months for a behavior to gain momentum and turn into a habit. Don‚Äôt give up just after a few days!<sup id=\"_ref-22\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 22\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Develop-Productive-Habits#_note-22\">[22]</a></sup></li> \n  <li>Create a ‚Äúclocking out‚Äù ritual by doing the same thing every day before you stop working. People talk about the importance of starting the day, but finishing your work the same way every day will help you compartmentalize and maintain a clear headspace.<sup id=\"_ref-23\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 23\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Develop-Productive-Habits#_note-23\">[23]</a></sup></li> \n  <li>There‚Äôs very little evidence that working longer hours will make you more productive. People tend to naturally spread their tasks out over a longer period of time if they have it in their head that they‚Äôre working late, so don‚Äôt worry about being the last one out of the office!<sup id=\"_ref-24\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 24\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Develop-Productive-Habits#_note-24\">[24]</a></sup></li>\n </ul> \n <h2><span title=\"Edit section: References\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"References\">References</span></h2>\n <div class=\"mw-references-wrap
